{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01C1zTHeCf1mrivxu3DoUVen","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! Now I see the issue very clearly:\n\n1. When a timeout occurs in azx_rirb_get_response:\n   - First, it sets `chip->polling_mode = 1` (line 912) and retries\n   - If that still fails, it tries to disable MSI (line 923)\n   - If that still fails, it sets `chip->single_cmd = 1` (line 951) and releases CORB/RIRB\n\n2. The problem is: After suspend/resume, these flags are NOT being reset:\n   - `chip->polling_mode` is not reset to 0\n   - `chip->single_cmd` is not reset to 0\n   - `chip->poll_count` is not reset to 0\n\n3. When azx_resume calls azx_init_chip(chip, 1), the RIRB is re-initialized via azx_init_cmd_io (line 1223). However, if chip->single_cmd is still 1, it skips this initialization!\n\nLooking at azx_init_chip again (lines 1222-1223):\n```c\nif (!chip->single_cmd)\n    azx_init_cmd_io(chip);\n```\n\nSo if single_cmd mode was enabled before suspend, the RIRB won't be re-initialized after resume! Now I understand the complete issue:1. `azx_init_cmd_io` initializes the CORB (Command Output Ring Buffer) and RIRB (Response Input Ring Buffer) for communication with the codec.2. On line 752, it resets the cmds array: `memset(chip->rirb.cmds, 0, sizeof(chip->rirb.cmds));`3. However, this function is NOT called if `chip->single_cmd` is 1 (as seen in line 1222-1223 of azx_init_chip).\n\nSo the bug is:\n1. During normal operation, a timeout occurs that causes the driver to enter polling_mode or single_cmd mode\n2. The system suspends to RAM\n3. During suspend, azx_stop_chip() sets chip->initialized = 0, but does NOT reset:   - chip->polling_mode\n   - chip->single_cmd\n   - chip->poll_count\n4. During resume, azx_init_chip() is called\n5. Since chip->single_cmd might still be 1, azx_init_cmd_io() is NOT called\n6. The RIRB is not re-initialized, so codec communication fails\n7. The codec doesn't respond to commands, causing timeouts and the \"choppy\" sound issue\n\nThe fix should be to reset these flags during suspend or resume:\n\n**Option 1**: Reset them in azx_suspend before stopping the chip\n**Option 2**: Reset them in azx_resume before initializing the chip\n**Option 3**: Reset them in azx_stop_chip \n\nLet me look at what's the most logical place. Since azx_stop_chip is called during suspend, and it already resets chip->initialized, it makes sense to also reset the other flags there.\n\nActually, wait. Let me check azx_stop_chip again. System suspends - `azx_suspend()` calls `azx_stop_chip()` which resets `chip->initialized` but **NOT** the error recovery flags\n3. System resumes - `azx_resume()` calls `azx_init_chip(chip, 1)` for full reset\n4. In `azx_init_chip()`, lines 1222-1223 check `if (!chip->single_cmd)` before calling `azx_init_cmd_io()`\n5. Since `single_cmd` is still 1 from before suspend, the CORB/RIRB are never re-initialized\n6.
